## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: nonlinear dynamics / classical mechanics (nonlinear oscillators)
**Analysis**: The target dv_dt is acceleration expressed as a function of state variables x (position), v (velocity), and possibly explicit time t, which is the standard form for second-order mechanical oscillator models. Common structures include restoring forces depending on x, damping terms depending on v, and external/parametric forcing depending on t.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Simple harmonic oscillator (undamped, unforced): dv_dt = c0 * x (linear restoring acceleration)
- Linear viscous damping oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (restoring + linear damping)
- Time-forced linear oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * sin(c3 * t) (external harmonic drive)
- Time-forced linear oscillator (cosine): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * cos(c3 * t) (alternative phase convention)
- Duffing oscillator (cubic stiffness): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (hardening/softening spring + damping)
- Driven Duffing: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * sin(c4 * t) (nonlinear stiffness + damping + drive)
- Pendulum equation (exact): dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * x) + c2 * v (restoring via sine of angle-like x, with damping)
- Quadratic (aero) damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v * Abs(v) (drag proportional to v|v|)
- Coulomb (dry) friction damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * sign(v) (constant-magnitude friction opposing motion)
- Van der Pol oscillator (state-dependent damping): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * (c2 - x**2) * v (negative damping at small x, positive at large x)
- Rayleigh oscillator (velocity-dependent damping): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * (c2 - v**2) * v (self-excited oscillation via nonlinear damping)
- Liénard-type oscillator (general nonlinear damping + restoring): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + (c2 + c3 * x**2) * v (polynomial restoring and damping)
- Parametric excitation (time-varying stiffness): dv_dt = (c0 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) * x + c3 * v (Mathieu-type parametric oscillator with damping)
- Nonlinear stiffness saturation (softening/hardening that levels off): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x / (1 + c2 * x**2) + c3 * v (bounded effective stiffness at large |x|)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Conservative (energy-preserving) oscillators often have dv_dt depending on x only (no v term); adding v terms typically introduces dissipation or self-excitation.
- Restoring forces are frequently odd in x (e.g., x, x**3, sin(c*x)); odd symmetry tends to yield symmetric oscillations about x=0.
- Damping forces are frequently odd in v (e.g., v, v*Abs(v), sign(v)); this enforces energy loss regardless of direction of motion.
- Self-excited limit cycles are commonly modeled by state-dependent damping factors multiplying v (e.g., (c0 - x**2)*v or (c0 - v**2)*v), which switch from negative to positive damping as amplitude grows.
- External forcing typically enters additively as a time-only term (e.g., sin(c*t), cos(c*t)), producing resonance and frequency-locking behaviors.
- Parametric excitation typically multiplies x with a time-periodic coefficient (c0 + c1*cos(c*t))*x, leading to parametric resonance bands.
- Hardening/softening stiffness is commonly represented by adding a cubic term in x (c*x**3), which shifts oscillation frequency with amplitude.
- Dry friction introduces non-smooth dynamics via sign(v) or piecewise terms, often causing stick-slip and waveform flattening near turning points.
- If dv_dt contains strong x*v cross-terms (e.g., x**2*v), it often indicates amplitude-dependent damping rather than a pure restoring force.
